-webkit-border-before	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The -webkit-border-before CSS property is a shorthand property for setting the individual logical block start border property values in a single place in the style sheet. -webkit-border-before can be used to set the values for one or more of: -webkit-border-before-width, -webkit-border-before-style, and -webkit-border-before-color. It maps to a physical border depending on the element's writing mode, directionality, and text orientation. It corresponds to the border-top, border-right, border-bottom, or border-left property depending on the values defined for writing-mode, direction, and text-orientation.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-width: as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-width: medium</li><li>border-right-width: medium</li><li>border-bottom-width: medium</li><li>border-left-width: medium</li></ul></li><li>border-style: as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-style: none</li><li>border-right-style: none</li><li>border-bottom-style: none</li><li>border-left-style: none</li></ul></li><li>color: variesFromBrowserToBrowser</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* Border values */\n-webkit-border-before: 1px;\n-webkit-border-before: 2px dotted;\n-webkit-border-before: medium dashed blue;\n\n/* Global values */\n-webkit-border-before: inherit;\n-webkit-border-before: initial;\n-webkit-border-before: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/-webkit-border-before

:-moz-focusring	A			css pseudo classes							<section class="prog__container"><p>The :-moz-focusring CSS pseudo-class is similar to the :focus pseudo-class, but it only matches an element if the element is currently focused and a focus ring or other indicator should be drawn for that element. If :-moz-focusring matches, then :focus also matches, but the converse is not always true - it depends on whether the user agent has focus ring drawing enabled and how the element was focused. Whether the user agent has focus ring drawing enabled can depend on things like the settings of the operating system the user is using, so the precise behavior of this pseudo-class can vary from platform to platform depending on each platforms' particular focus best practices (defaults) or user modified settings.</p><pre><code>:-moz-focusring</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/:-moz-focusring

This pseudo-class is applied according to the following rules:If the control does not have focus, and the value is invalid, apply this pseudo-class., If the control has focus, and the value was valid (including empty) when it gained focus, do not apply the pseudo-class., If the control has focus, and the value was invalid when it gained focus, re-validate on every keystroke., If the element is required, the preceding rules apply only if the user has changed the value or attempted to submit the form.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/:-moz-ui-invalid

:valid	A			css pseudo classes							<section class="prog__container"><p>The :valid CSS pseudo-class represents any input or form element whose content validates correctly according to the input's type setting. :visited	A			css pseudo classes							<section class="prog__container"><p>The :visited CSS pseudo-class lets you select only links that have been visited. This style may be overridden by any other link-related pseudo-classes, that is :link, :hover, and :active, appearing in subsequent rules. In order to style appropriately links, you need to put the :visited rule after the :link rule but before the other ones, defined in the LVHA-order: :link — :visited — :hover — :active.</p><pre><code>:visited { style properties }</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/:visited
<angle>	A			css data types							<section class="prog__container"><p>The <angle> CSS data type represents angle values. Positive angles represent clockwise angles, negative angles represent counterclockwise angles. Its syntax is a <number> data type immediately followed by the unit (deg, grad, rad or turn). Like for any CSS dimension, there is no space between the unit literal and the number.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/angle
<basic-shape>	A			css data types							<section class="prog__container"><p>The <basic-shape> type can be specified using basic shape functions. When using this syntax to define shapes, the reference box is defined by each property that uses <basic-shape> values. The coordinate system for the shape has its origin on the top-left corner of the reference box with the x-axis running to the right and the y-axis running downwards. All the lengths expressed in percentages are resolved from the used dimensions of the reference box.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/basic-shape

<color>	A			css data types							<section class="prog__container"><p>The <color> CSS data type denotes a color in the sRGB color space. A color can be described in any of these ways:using a keyword, using the RGB cubic-coordinate system (via the #-hexadecimal or the rgb() and rgba() functional notations), using the HSL cylindrical-coordinate system (via the hsl() and hsla() functional notations)</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/color_value
<custom-ident>	A			css data types							<section class="prog__container"><p>The <custom-ident> CSS data value denotes an arbitrary user-defined string used as an identifier. <gradient>	A			css data types							<section class="prog__container"><p>The gradient CSS data type denotes a CSS image made of a progressive transition between two or more colors. Its concrete size will match the one of the element it applies to.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/gradient

animation-fill-mode	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The animation-fill-mode CSS property specifies how a CSS animation should apply styles to its target before and after it is executing.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>none</em></p><pre><code>animation-fill-mode: none;\nanimation-fill-mode: forwards;\nanimation-fill-mode: backwards;\nanimation-fill-mode: both;\n\n/* Several values may be given, separated by commas. */\n/* Each applies for each animation in animation-name. */\nanimation-fill-mode: none, backwards;\nanimation-fill-mode: both, forwards, none;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/animation-fill-mode
animation-fill-mode property	R	animation-fill-mode										
animation-iteration-count	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The animation-iteration-count CSS property defines the number of times an animation cycle should be played before stopping. If multiple values are specified, each time the animation is played, the next value in the list is used, cycling back to the first value after the last one is used.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>1</em></p><pre><code>animation-iteration-count: infinite;\nanimation-iteration-count: 3;\nanimation-iteration-count: 2.3;\n\nanimation-iteration-count: 2, 0, infinite;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/animation-iteration-count

animation-name	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The animation-name CSS property specifies a list of animations that should be applied to the selected element. Each name indicates a @keyframes at-rule that defines the property values for the animation sequence.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>none</em></p><pre><code>animation-name: none;\nanimation-name: test_05;\nanimation-name: -specific;\nanimation-name: sliding-vertically;\n\nanimation-name: test1;\nanimation-name: test1, animation4;\nanimation-name: none, -moz-specific, sliding;\n\nanimation-name: initial\nanimation-name: inherit\nanimation-name: unset\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/animation-name

animation-play-state	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The animation-play-state CSS property determines whether an animation is running or paused. This can be queried to determine whether or not the animation is currently running. In addition, its value can be set to pause and resume playback of an animation.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>running</em></p><pre><code>/* Single animation */\nanimation-play-state: running;\nanimation-play-state: paused;\n\n/* Multiple animations */\nanimation-play-state: paused, running, running;\n\n/* Global values */\nanimation-play-state: inherit;\nanimation-play-state: initial;\nanimation-play-state: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/animation-play-state

animation-timing-function	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The animation-timing-function CSS property specifies how a CSS animation should progress over the duration of each cycle. backface-visibility	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The CSS backface-visibility property determines whether or not the back face of the element is visible when facing the user. The back face of an element is always a transparent background, letting, when visible, a mirror image of the front face be displayed.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>visible</em></p><pre><code>backface-visibility: visible;\nbackface-visibility: hidden;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/backface-visibility

background	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The background CSS property is a shorthand for setting the individual background values in a single place in the style sheet. background can be used to set the values for one or more of: background-clip, background-color, background-image, background-origin, background-position, background-repeat, background-size, and background-attachment.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>background-image: none</li><li>background-position: 0% 0%</li><li>background-size: auto auto</li><li>background-repeat: repeat</li><li>background-origin: padding-box</li><li>background-clip: border-box</li><li>background-attachment: scroll</li><li>background-color: transparent</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* Using a <background-color> */\nbackground: green;\n\n/* Using a <bg-image> and <repeat-style> */\nbackground: url("test.jpg") repeat-y;\n\n/* Using a <box> and <background-color> */\nbackground: border-box red;\n\n/* A single image, centered and scaled */\nbackground: no-repeat center/80% url("../img/image.png");\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/background
background property	R	background

background-size	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The background-size CSS property specifies the size of the background images. border-block-end	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-block-end CSS property is a shorthand property for setting the individual logical block end border property values in a single place in the style sheet. border-block-end can be used to set the values for one or more of: border-block-end-width, border-block-end-style, border-block-end-color. It maps to a physical border depending on the element's writing mode, directionality, and text orientation. It corresponds to the border-top, border-right, border-bottom, or border-left property depending on the values defined for writing-mode, direction, and text-orientation.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-width: as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-width: medium</li><li>border-right-width: medium</li><li>border-bottom-width: medium</li><li>border-left-width: medium</li></ul></li><li>border-style: as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-style: none</li><li>border-right-style: none</li><li>border-bottom-style: none</li><li>border-left-style: none</li></ul></li><li>color: Varies from one browser to another</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>border-block-end: 1px;\nborder-block-end: 2px dotted;\nborder-block-end: medium dashed blue;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-block-end

border-bottom-left-radius	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-bottom-left-radius CSS property sets the rounding of the bottom-left corner of the element. The rounding can be a circle or an ellipse, or if one of the value is 0 no rounding is done and the corner is square.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>0</em></p><pre><code>/* the corner is a circle */\n/* border-bottom-left-radius: radius */\nborder-bottom-left-radius: 3px;\n\n/* the corner is an ellipsis */\n/* border-bottom-left-radius: horizontal vertical */\nborder-bottom-left-radius: 0.5em 1em;\n\nborder-bottom-left-radius: inherit;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-bottom-left-radius
border-bottom-left-radius property	R	border-bottom-left-radius										
border-bottom-right-radius	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-bottom-right-radius CSS property sets the rounding of the bottom-right corner of the element. The rounding can be a circle or an ellipse, or if one of the value is 0 no rounding is done and the corner is square.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>0</em></p><pre><code>/* the corner is a circle */\n/* border-bottom-right-radius: radius */\nborder-bottom-right-radius: 3px;\n\n/* the corner is an ellipsis */\n/* border-bottom-right-radius: horizontal vertical */\nborder-bottom-right-radius: 0.5em 1em;\n\nborder-bottom-right-radius: inherit;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-bottom-right-radius
border-bottom-right-radius property	R	border-bottom-right-radius										
border-bottom-style	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-bottom-style CSS property sets the line style of the bottom border of a box.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>none</em></p><pre><code>border-bottom-style: none;\nborder-bottom-style: hidden;\nborder-bottom-style: dotted;\nborder-bottom-style: dashed;\nborder-bottom-style: solid;\nborder-bottom-style: double;\nborder-bottom-style: groove;\nborder-bottom-style: ridge;\nborder-bottom-style: inset;\nborder-bottom-style: outset;\n\nborder-bottom-style: inherit;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-bottom-style
border-bottom-style property	R	border-bottom-style										
border-bottom-width	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p> </p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>medium</em></p><pre><code>/* Any <length> value */\nborder-bottom-width: 10em;\nborder-bottom-width: 3vmax;\nborder-bottom-width: 6px;\n\n/* A keyword */\nborder-bottom-width: thin;\nborder-bottom-width: medium;\nborder-bottom-width: thick;\n\nborder-bottom-width: inherit;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-bottom-width

border-collapse	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-collapse CSS property determines whether a table's borders are separated or collapsed. In the separated model, adjacent cells each have their own distinct borders. In the collapsed model, adjacent table cells share borders.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>separate</em></p><pre><code>border-collapse: collapse;\nborder-collapse: separate;\n\nborder-collapse: inherit;</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-collapse
border-collapse property	R	border-collapse										
border-color	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-color CSS property is a shorthand for setting the color of the four sides of an element's border: border-top-color, border-right-color, border-bottom-color, border-left-color</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-color: currentcolor</li><li>border-right-color: currentcolor</li><li>border-bottom-color: currentcolor</li><li>border-left-color: currentcolor</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* border-color: color */ /* the color applies to all sides */ \nborder-color: red;\n\n/* border-color: top&bottom right&left */\nborder-color: red #f015ca;\n\n/* border-color: top right&left bottom */\nborder-color: red yellow green;\n\n/* border-color: top right bottom left */\nborder-color: red yellow green blue;\n\nborder-color: inherit;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-color
border-color property	R	border-color										
border-image	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-image CSS property allows drawing an image on the borders of elements. This makes drawing complex looking widgets much simpler than it has been and removes the need for nine boxes in some cases. The border-image is used instead of the border styles given by the border-style properties. Though the specification requires that border-style must be present if border-image is used, some browsers may not implement this.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-image-source: none</li><li>border-image-slice: 100%</li><li>border-image-width: 1</li><li>border-image-outset: 0s</li><li>border-image-repeat: stretch</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* image-source | height | width | repeat */\nborder-image: url("/images/border.png") 30 30 repeat;\nborder-image: url("/images/border.png") 30 30 stretch;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-image
border-image property	R	border-image										
border-image-outset	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-image-outset property describes by what amount the border image area extends beyond the border box.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>0s</em></p><pre><code>/* border-image-outset: sides */\nborder-image-outset: 1.5;\n\n/* border-image-outset: vertical horizontal */\nborder-image-outset: 1 1.2;\n\n/* border-image-outset: top horizontal bottom */\nborder-image-outset: 30px 2 45px;\n\n/* border-image-outset: top right bottom left */\nborder-image-outset: 7px 12px 14px 5px;\n\nborder-image-outset: inherit;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-image-outset
border-image-outset property	R	border-image-outset										
border-image-repeat	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-image-repeat CSS property defines how the middle part of a border image is handled so that it can match the size of the border. It has a one-value syntax that describes the behavior of all the sides, and a two-value syntax that sets a different value for the horizontal and vertical behavior.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>stretch</em></p><pre><code>/* border-image-repeat: type */\nborder-image-repeat: stretch;\n\n/* border-image-repeat: horizontal vertical */\nborder-image-repeat: round stretch;\n\n/* Global values */\nborder-image-repeat: inherit;\nborder-image-repeat: initial;\nborder-image-repeat: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-image-repeat
border-image-repeat property	R	border-image-repeat										
border-image-slice	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-image-slice CSS property divides the image specified by border-image-source in nine regions: the four corners, the four edges and the middle. It does this by specifying 4 inwards offsets.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>100%</em></p><pre><code>/* border-image-slice: slice */\nborder-image-slice: 30%; \n\n/* border-image-slice: horizontal vertical */\nborder-image-slice: 10% 30%;\n\n/* border-image-slice: top horizontal bottom */\nborder-image-slice: 30 30% 45;\n\n/* border-image-slice: top right bottom left */\nborder-image-slice: 7 12 14 5; \n\n/* border-image-slice: … fill */\n/* The fill value can be placed between any value */\nborder-image-slice: 10% fill 7 12;\n\n/* Global values */\nborder-image-slice: inherit;\nborder-image-slice: initial;\nborder-image-slice: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-image-slice
border-image-slice property	R	border-image-slice										
border-image-source	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-image-source CSS property defines the <image> to use instead of the style of the border. If this property is set to none, the style defined by border-style is used instead.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>none</em></p><pre><code>/* no border-image, use the specified border-style */\nborder-image-source: none;\n\n/* the image.jpg is used as image */\nborder-image-source: url(image.jpg);\n\n/* a gradient is used as image */\nborder-image-source: linear-gradient(to top, red, yellow);\n\n/* Global values */\nborder-image-source: inherit;\nborder-image-source: initial;\nborder-image-source: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-image-source
border-image-source property	R	border-image-source										
border-image-width	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-image-width CSS property defines the width of the border image by defining inward offsets from the border edges. If the border-image-width is greater than the border-width, then the border image extends beyond the padding (and/or content) edge.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>1</em></p><pre><code>/* border-image-width: all */\nborder-image-width: 3;\n\n/* border-image-width: vertical horizontal */\nborder-image-width: 2em 3em;\n\n/* border-image-width: top horizontal bottom */\nborder-image-width: 5% 15% 10%;\n\n/* border-image-width: top right bottom left */\nborder-image-width: 5% 2em 10% auto;\n\n/* Global values */\nborder-image-width: inherit;\nborder-image-width: initial;\nborder-image-width: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-image-width
border-image-width property	R	border-image-width										
border-inline-end	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-inline-end CSS property is a shorthand property for setting the individual logical inline end border property values in a single place in the style sheet. border-inline-end can be used to set the values for one or more of: border-inline-end-width, border-inline-end-style, border-inline-end-color. It maps to a physical border depending on the element's writing mode, directionality, and text orientation. It corresponds to the border-top, border-right, border-bottom, or border-left property depending on the values defined for writing-mode, direction, and text-orientation.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-width: as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-width: medium</li><li>border-right-width: medium</li><li>border-bottom-width: medium</li><li>border-left-width: medium</li></ul></li><li>border-style: as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-style: none</li><li>border-right-style: none</li><li>border-bottom-style: none</li><li>border-left-style: none</li></ul></li><li>color: Varies from one browser to another</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>border-inline-end: 1px;\nborder-inline-end: 2px dashed;\nborder-inline-end: medium dashed blue;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-inline-end
border-inline-end-color	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-inline-end-color CSS property defines the color of the logical inline end border of an element, which maps to a physical border color depending on the element's writing mode, directionality, and text orientation. It corresponds to the border-top-color, border-right-color, border-bottom-color, or border-left-color property depending on the values defined for writing-mode, direction, and text-orientation.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>currentcolor</em></p><pre><code>border-inline-end-color: rebeccapurple;\nborder-inline-end-color: #663399;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-inline-end-color

border-radius	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The border-radius CSS property allows Web authors to define how rounded border corners are. The curve of each corner is defined using one or two radii, defining its shape: circle or ellipse.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>border-top-left-radius: 0</li><li>border-top-right-radius: 0</li><li>border-bottom-right-radius: 0</li><li>border-bottom-left-radius: 0</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* The syntax of the first radius allows one to four values */\n/* Radius is set for all 4 sides */\nborder-radius: 10px;\n\n/* top-left-and-bottom-right | top-right-and-bottom-left */\nborder-radius: 10px 5%;\n\n/* top-left | top-right-and-bottom-left | bottom-right */\nborder-radius: 2px 4px 2px;\n\n/* top-left | top-right | bottom-right | bottom-left */\nborder-radius: 1px 0 3px 4px;\n\n/* The syntax of the second radius allows one to four values */\n/* (first radius values) / radius */\nborder-radius: 10px 5% / 20px;\n\n/* (first radius values) / top-left-and-bottom-right | top-right-and-bottom-left */\nborder-radius: 10px 5% / 20px 30px;\n\n/* (first radius values) / top-left | top-right-and-bottom-left | bottom-right */\nborder-radius: 10px 5px 2em / 20px 25px 30%;\n\n/* (first radius values) / top-left | top-right | bottom-right | bottom-left */\nborder-radius: 10px 5% / 20px 25em 30px 35em;\n\nborder-radius: inherit;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/border-radius

box-shadow	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The box-shadow property describes one or more shadow effects as a comma-separated list. brightness()	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>Applies a linear multiplier to input image, making it appear more or less bright. A value of 0% will create an image that is completely black. A value of 100% leaves the input unchanged. Other values are linear multipliers on the effect. column-width	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The column-width CSS property suggests an optimal column width. The column-width is the maximum width a column will become before adding another column. For instance, a 300px column width a gap of 0px would be a single column at 599px, but at 600px it would be split into 2 columns. This allows us to achieve scalable designs that fit different screen sizes. Especially in presence of the column-count CSS property which has precedence, to set an exact column width, all length values must be specified. In horizontal text these are width, column-width, column-gap, and column-rule-width.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>auto</em></p><pre><code>/* Keyword value */\ncolumn-width: auto;\n\n/* Different <length> values */\ncolumn-width: 6px;\ncolumn-width: 25em;\ncolumn-width: 0.3vw;\n\n/* Global values */\ncolumn-width: inherit;\ncolumn-width: initial;\ncolumn-width: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/column-width

contrast()	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>Adjusts the contrast of the input. A value of 0% will create an image that is completely gray. A value of 100% leaves the input unchanged. Values of amount over 100% are allowed, providing results with more contrast. The lacuna value for interpolation is 1.</p><pre><code>filter: contrast(200%)\n<svg style="position: absolute; top: -99999px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n <filter id="contrast">\n <feComponentTransfer>\n <feFuncR type="linear" slope="[amount]" intercept="-(0.5 * [amount]) + 0.5"/>\n <feFuncG type="linear" slope="[amount]" intercept="-(0.5 * [amount]) + 0.5"/>\n <feFuncB type="linear" slope="[amount]" intercept="-(0.5 * [amount]) + 0.5"/>\n </feComponentTransfer>\n </filter>\n</svg>\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/filter#contrast()_2

drop-shadow()	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>Applies a drop shadow effect to the input image. A drop shadow is effectively a blurred, offset version of the input image's alpha mask drawn in a particular color, composited below the image. The function accepts a parameter of type <shadow> (defined in CSS3 Backgrounds), with the exception that the ‘inset’ keyword is not allowed. This function is similar to the more established box-shadow property; the difference is that with filters, some browsers provide hardware acceleration for better performance. The parameters of the <shadow> parameter are as follows.</p><pre><code>\n <offset-x> <offset-y> (required)\n These are two <length> values to set the shadow offset. <offset-x> specifies the horizontal distance. Negative values place the shadow to the left of the element. <offset-y> specifies the vertical distance. Negative values place the shadow above the element. See <length> for possible units.\n If both values are 0, the shadow is placed behind the element (and may generate a blur effect if <blur-radius> and/or <spread-radius> is set).\n <blur-radius> (optional)\n This is a third <length> value. The larger this value, the bigger the blur, so the shadow becomes bigger and lighter. Negative values are not allowed. If not specified, it will be 0 (the shadow's edge is sharp).\n <spread-radius> (optional)\n This is a fourth <length> value. Positive values will cause the shadow to expand and grow bigger, and negative values will cause the shadow to shrink. If not specified, it will be 0 (the shadow will be the same size as the element). \n Note: Webkit, and maybe other browsers, do not support this 4th length; it will not render if added.\n <color> (optional)\n See <color> values for possible keywords and notations. If not specified, the color depends on the browser. In Gecko (Firefox), Presto (Opera) and Trident (Internet Explorer), the value of the color property is used. On the other hand, WebKit's shadow is transparent and therefore useless if <color> is omitted.\nfilter: drop-shadow(16px 16px 10px black)<svg style="position: absolute; top: -999999px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">\n <filter id="drop-shadow">\n <feGaussianBlur in="SourceAlpha" stdDeviation="[radius]"/>\n <feOffset dx="[offset-x]" dy="[offset-y]" result="offsetblur"/>\n <feFlood flood-color="[color]"/>\n <feComposite in2="offsetblur" operator="in"/>\n <feMerge>\n <feMergeNode/>\n <feMergeNode in="SourceGraphic"/>\n </feMerge>\n </filter>\n</svg>\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/filter#drop-shadow()_2

fallback	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The fallback descriptor can be used to specify a counter style to fall back to if the current counter style cannot create a marker representation for a particular counter value. If the specified fallback style is also unable to construct a representation, then its fallback style will be used. If a valid fallback style is not specified, it defaults to decimal. A few scenarios where fallback style will be used are:When the range descriptor is specified for a counter style, the fallback style will be used to represent values that fall outside the range., When the fixed system is used and there are not enough symbols to cover all the list items, the fallback style will be used for the rest of the list items.</p><pre><code>/* Keyword values */\nfallback: lower-alpha;\nfallback: custom-gangnam-style;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/@counter-style/fallback

flex	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The flex CSS property is a shorthand property specifying the ability of a flex item to alter its dimensions to fill available space. flexible boxes	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The CSS3 Flexible Box, or flexbox, is a layout mode providing for the arrangement of elements on a page such that the elements behave predictably when the page layout must accommodate different screen sizes and different display devices. For many applications, the flexible box model provides an improvement over the block model in that it does not use floats, nor do the flex container's margins collapse with the margins of its contents.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/CSS_Flexible_Box_Layout/Using_CSS_flexible_boxes

font	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The font CSS property is either a shorthand property for setting font-style, font-variant, font-weight, font-size, line-height and font-family, or a way to set the element's font to a system font, using specific keywords.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>font-style: normal</li><li>font-variant: normal</li><li>font-weight: normal</li><li>font-stretch: normal</li><li>font-size: medium</li><li>line-height: normal</li><li>font-family: depends on user agent</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* size | family */\nfont: 2em "Open Sans", sans-serif;\n\n/* style | size | family */\nfont: italic 2em "Open Sans", sans-serif;\n\n/* style | variant | weight | size/line-height | family */\nfont: italic small-caps bolder 16px/3 cursive;\n\n/* style | variant | weight | stretch | size/line-height | family */\nfont: italic small-caps bolder condensed 16px/3 cursive;\n\n/* The font used in system dialogs */\nfont: message-box;\nfont: icon;\n\n/* Global values */\nfont: inherit;\nfont: initial;\nfont: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/font

font-family	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The font-family CSS property lets you specify a prioritized list of font family names and/or generic family names for the selected element. Values are separated by a comma to indicate that they are alternatives. font-size-adjust	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The font-size-adjust CSS property specifies that font size should be chosen based on the height of lowercase letters rather than the height of capital letters. grayscale()	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>Converts the input image to grayscale. The value of ‘amount’ defines the proportion of the conversion. grid	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The grid CSS property is a shorthand property that sets all of the explicit grid properties (grid-template-rows, grid-template-columns, and grid-template-areas), all the implicit grid properties (grid-auto-rows, grid-auto-columns, and grid-auto-flow), and the gutter properties (grid-column-gap and grid-row-gap) in a single declaration.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>grid-template-rows: none</li><li>grid-template-columns: none</li><li>grid-template-areas: none</li><li>grid-auto-rows: auto</li><li>grid-auto-columns: auto</li><li>grid-auto-flow: row</li><li>grid-column-gap: 0</li><li>grid-row-gap: 0</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* <'grid-template'> values */\ngrid: none;\ngrid: "a" 100px "b" 1fr;\ngrid: [linename1] "a" 100px [linename2];\ngrid: "a" 200px "b" min-content;\ngrid: "a" minmax(100px, max-content) "b" 20%;\ngrid: 100px / 200px;\ngrid: minmax(400px, min-content) / repeat(auto-fill, 50px);\n\n/* <'grid-template-rows'> /\n [ auto-flow && dense? ] <'grid-auto-columns'>? values */\ngrid: 200px / auto-flow;\ngrid: 30% / auto-flow dense;\ngrid: repeat(3, [line1 line2 line3] 200px) / auto-flow 300px;\ngrid: [line1] minmax(20em, max-content) / auto-flow dense 40%;\n\n/* [ auto-flow && dense? ] <'grid-auto-rows'>? /\n <'grid-template-columns'> values */\ngrid: auto-flow / 200px;\ngrid: auto-flow dense / 30%;\ngrid: auto-flow 300px / repeat(3, [line1 line2 line3] 200px);\ngrid: auto-flow dense 40% / [line1] minmax(20em, max-content);\n\n/* Global values */\ngrid: inherit;\ngrid: initial;\ngrid: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/grid
grid-area	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The grid-area CSS property is a shorthand property for grid-row-start, grid-row-end, grid-column-start and grid-column-end, specifying a grid item’s size and location within the grid row by contributing a line, a span, or nothing (automatic) to its grid placement, thereby specifying the edges of its grid area.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>grid-row-start: auto</li><li>grid-column-start: auto</li><li>grid-row-end: auto</li><li>grid-column-end: auto</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* Keyword values */\ngrid-area: auto;\ngrid-area: auto / auto;\ngrid-area: auto / auto / auto;\ngrid-area: auto / auto / auto / auto;\n\n/* <custom-ident> values */\ngrid-area: some-grid-area;\ngrid-area: some-grid-area / another-grid-area;\n\n/* <integer> && <custom-ident>? values */\ngrid-area: some-grid-area 4;\ngrid-area: some-grid-area 4 / 2 another-grid-area;\n\n/* span && [ <integer> || <custom-ident> ] values */\ngrid-area: span 3;\ngrid-area: span 3 / span some-grid-area;\ngrid-area: 2 span / another-grid-area span;\n\n/* Global values */\ngrid-area: inherit;\ngrid-area: initial;\ngrid-area: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/grid-area

hsl()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>Colors also can be defined the Hue-saturation-lightness model (HSL) using the hsl() functional notation.  The advantage of HSL over RGB is that it is far more intuitive: you can guess at the colors you want, and then tweak. It is also easier to create sets of matching colors (by keeping the hue the same and varying the lightness/darkness, and saturation).Hue is represented as an angle of the color circle (i.e. the rainbow represented in a circle). This angle is given as a unitless <number>. By definition red=0=360, and the other colors are spread around the circle, so green=120, blue=240, etc. As an angle, it implicitly wraps around such that -120=240 and 480=120.Saturation and lightness are represented as percentages.\n 100% is full saturation, and0% is a shade of grey.\n 100% lightness is white, 0% lightness is black, and 50% lightness is "normal".</p><pre><code>\nNote: In the CSS Color Module Level 4 spec, hsla() has been defined as an legacy function with identical grammar and behaviour to hsl(); in effect, an alias. Going forward, both can accept exactly the same parameters.\nhsl(0, 100%,50%) /* red */ \nhsl(30, 100%,50%)   \nhsl(60, 100%,50%)   \nhsl(90, 100%,50%)   \nhsl(120,100%,50%) /* green */ \nhsl(150,100%,50%)   \nhsl(180,100%,50%)   \nhsl(210,100%,50%)   \nhsl(240,100%,50%) /* blue */ \nhsl(270,100%,50%)   \nhsl(300,100%,50%)   \nhsl(330,100%,50%)   \nhsl(360,100%,50%) /* red */ \n\nhsl(120,100%,25%) /* dark green */ \nhsl(120,100%,50%) /* green */ \nhsl(120,100%,75%) /* light green */ \n\nhsl(120,100%,50%) /* green */ \nhsl(120, 67%,50%)   \nhsl(120, 33%,50%)   \nhsl(120, 0%,50%)   \n\nhsl(120, 60%,70%) /* pastel green */ \n\n/* whitespace syntax */\nhsl(120 60% 70%) /* pastel green */ \n\n/* angle values for hue component; also accepts rad, grad, turn */\nhsl(120deg 60% 70%) /* pastel green */ \n\n/* optional alpha value */\nhsl(240,100%,50%,0.05) /* 5% opaque blue */ \nhsl(240,100%,50%,5%) /* 5% opaque blue with percentage value for alpha */ \nhsl(240 100% 50% / 0.05) /* 5% opaque blue */ \nhsl(240 100% 50% / 5%) /* 5% opaque blue with percentage value for alpha */\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/color_value#hsl()
hsla()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>Colors can be defined in the hue-saturation-lightness-alpha model (HSLa) using the hsla() functional notation. HSLa extends the HSL color model to include the alpha channel, allowing specification of the opacity of a color.\n a means opacity: 0=transparent; 1=opaque;</p><pre><code>hsla(240,100%,50%,0.05) /* 5% opaque blue */ \nhsla(240,100%,50%, 0.4) /* 40% opaque blue */ \nhsla(240,100%,50%, 0.7) /* 70% opaque blue */ \nhsla(240,100%,50%, 1) /* full opaque blue */ \n\n/* whitespace syntax */\nhsla(240 100% 50% / 0.05) /* 5% opaque blue */ \n\n/* percentage value for alpha */\nhsla(240 100% 50% / 5%) /* 5% opaque blue */ \n\n/* angle values for hue component; also accepts rad, grad, turn */\nhsla(240deg 100% 50% / 5%) /* 5% opaque blue */ \nhsla(240deg,100%,50%, 0.4) /* 40% opaque blue */ \n\nNote: In the CSS Color Module Level 4 spec, hsla() has been defined as an legacy function with identical grammar and behaviour to hsl(); in effect, an alias. Going forward, both can accept exactly the same parameters.\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/color_value#hsla()

invert()	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>Inverts the samples in the input image. The value of ‘amount’ defines the proportion of the conversion. A value of 100% is completely inverted. linear-gradient()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>The CSS linear-gradient() function creates an <image> which represents a linear gradient of colors. The result of this function is an object of the CSS <gradient> data type. Like any other gradient, a CSS linear gradient is not a CSS <color> but an image with no intrinsic dimensions; that is, it has neither natural or preferred size, nor ratio. Its concrete size will match the size of the element it applies to.</p><pre><code>linear-gradient( 45deg, blue, red ); /* A gradient on 45deg axis starting blue and finishing red */\nlinear-gradient( to left top, blue, red); /* A gradient going from the bottom right to the top left starting blue and \n finishing red */\n\nlinear-gradient( 0deg, blue, green 40%, red ); /* A gradient going from the bottom to top, starting blue, being green after 40% \n and finishing red */ \n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/linear-gradient

max-block-size	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The max-block-size CSS property defines the horizontal or vertical maximal size of an element's block depending on its writing mode. It corresponds to the max-width or the max-height property, depending on the value defined for writing-mode. If the writing mode is vertically oriented, the value of max-block-size relates to the maximal width of the element, otherwise it relates to the maximal height of the element. It relates to max-inline-size, which defines the other dimension of the element.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>0</em></p><pre><code>/* <length> values */\nmax-block-size: 300px;\nmax-block-size: 25em;\n\n/* <percentage> values */\nmax-block-size: 75%;\n\n/* Keyword values */\nmax-block-size: none;\nmax-block-size: max-content;\nmax-block-size: min-content;\nmax-block-size: fit-content;\nmax-block-size: fill-available;\n\n/* Global values */\nmax-block-size: inherit;\nmax-block-size: initial;\nmax-block-size: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/max-block-size

minmax()	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The minmax() CSS function defines a size range greater than or equal to min and less than or equal to max. negative	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>When defining custom counter styles, the negative descriptor lets the author alter the representations of negative counter values, by providing a way to specify symbols to be appended or prepended to the counter representation when the value is negative. If the counter value is negative, the symbol provided as value for the descriptor will be prepended to the counter representation; and a second symbol if specified, will be appended to the representation. The negative descriptor has effect only if the system value is symbolic, alphabetic, numeric, additive, or extends, if the extended counter style itself uses a negative sign. If the negative descriptor is specified for other systems that don't support negative counter values, then the descriptor is ignored.</p><pre><code>/* <symbol> values */\nnegative: "-"; /* Prepends '-' if value is negative */\nnegative: "(" ")"; /* Surrounds value by '(' and ')' if it is negative */\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/@counter-style/negative

opacity()	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>Applies transparency to the samples in the input image. The value of ‘amount’ defines the proportion of the conversion. A value of 0% is completely transparent. A value of 100% leaves the input unchanged. Values between 0% and 100% are linear multipliers on the effect. This is equivalent to multiplying the input image samples by amount. The lacuna value for interpolation is 1. This function is similar to the more established opacity property; the difference is that with filters, some browsers provide hardware acceleration for better performance.</p><pre><code>filter: opacity(50%)</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/filter#opacity()_2

pad	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The pad descriptor can be used with custom counter style definitions when you need the marker representations to have a minimum length. If a marker representation is smaller than the specified pad length, then the marker will be padded with the specified pad symbol. Marker representations longer than the pad length are constructed as normal. Pad descriptor takes the minimum marker length as an integer and a symbol to be used for padding as the second parameter. A common usage of the pad descriptor is when you need your list to start numbering from 01 and go through 02, 03 and so on, instead of just 1, 2, 3...</p><pre><code>pad: 3 "0";\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/@counter-style/pad

rad	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>rad represents an angle in radians.  One full circle is 2π radians which approximates to 6.2832rad. 1rad is 180/π degrees. E.g. 0rad, 1.0708rad, 6.2832rad.</p><pre><code> A right angle: 90deg = 100grad = 0.25turn ≈ 1.5708rad\n A flat angle: 180deg = 200grad = 0.5turn ≈ 3.1416rad\n A right angle (towards the left): -90deg = -100grad = -0.25turn ≈ -1.5708rad\n A null angle: 0 = 0deg = 0grad = 0turn = 0rad\n\n Note: For zero angles the unit identifier is optional.\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/angle#rad

radial-gradient()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>The CSS radial-gradient() function creates an image which represents a gradient of colors radiating from an origin, the center of the gradient. The result of this function is an object of the CSS gradient data type.</p><pre><code>// Definition of the ending shape\nradial-gradient( circle, … ) /* Synonym of radial-gradient( circle farthest-corner, … ) */\nradial-gradient( ellipse, … ) /* Synonym of radial-gradient( ellipse farthest-corner, … ) */\nradial-gradient( <extent-keyword>, … ) /* It draws a circle */\nradial-gradient( circle radius, … ) /* A centered circle of the given length. It can't be a percentage */\nradial-gradient( ellipse x-axis y-axis, … ) /* The two semi-major axes are given, horizontal, then vertical */\n\n// Definition of the position of the shape\nradial-gradient ( … at <position>, … )\n\n// Definition of the color stops\nradial-gradient ( …, <color-stop>, … )\nradial-gradient ( …, <color-stop>, <color-stop> )</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/radial-gradient

repeating-linear-gradient	R	repeating-linear-gradient()										
repeating-linear-gradient function	R	repeating-linear-gradient()										
repeating-linear-gradient()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>The CSS repeating-linear-gradient function creates an <image> consisting of repeating gradients. It works similarly to the basic linear gradients as described by linear-gradient(), and takes the same arguments. However, it automatically repeats the color stops infinitely in both directions. The color stops' positions shift by multiples of the length of a basic linear gradient (the difference between the last color stops' position and the first).</p><pre><code>repeating-linear-gradient(45deg, blue, red); /* A repeating gradient on 45deg axe starting blue and finishing red */\nrepeating-linear-gradient(to left top, blue, red); /* A repeating gradient going from the bottom right to the top left \n starting blue and finishing red */\n\nrepeating-linear-gradient(0deg, blue, green 40%, red); /* A repeating gradient going from the bottom to top, starting blue, \n being green after 40% and finishing red */ \n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient
repeating-radial-gradient	R	repeating-radial-gradient()

repeating-radial-gradient()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>This works similarly to the standard radial gradients as described by radial-gradient(), but it automatically repeats the color stops infinitely in both directions, with their positions shifted by multiples of the difference between the last color stop's position and the first one's position.</p><pre><code>Definition of the ending shape\nrepeating-radial-gradient( circle, … ) /* Synonym of repeating-radial-gradient( circle farthest-corner, …) */\nrepeating-radial-gradient( ellipse, … ) /* Synonym of repeating-radial-gradient( ellipse farthest-corner, …) */\nrepeating-radial-gradient( <extent-keyword>, … ) /* It draws concentric circles */\nrepeating-radial-gradient( circle radius, … ) /* Concentrinc centered circles of the given length. It can't be in %. */\nrepeating-radial-gradient( ellipse x-axis y-axis, … ) /* The two semi-major axis are given, horizontal, then vertical */\n\nDefinition of the position of the shape\nrepeating-radial-gradient (… at <position>, … )\n\nDefinition of the color stops\nrepeating-radial-gradient (…, <color-stop>)\nrepeating-radial-gradient (…, <color-stop>, <color-stop>)\n\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-radial-gradient
replaced element	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>In CSS, a replaced element is an element whose representation is outside the scope of CSS. These are a type of external object whose representation is independent of the CSS. Typical replaced elements are img, object, video or form elements like textarea and input. Some elements, like audio or canvas are replaced elements only in specific cases. Objects inserted using the CSS content properties are anonymous replaced elements.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Replaced_element

revert	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The revert CSS keyword rolls back the cascade so that the property takes on the value it would have had if there were no styles in the current style origin (author, user, or user-agent). In author stylesheets (the normal case), for the purposes of the given declaration, it's as if there were no author-level styles, thus resetting the property to the default value established by the user-agent stylesheet (or by user styles, if any exist).</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/revert
rgb()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>Colors can be defined using the red-green-blue (RGB) model in two ways:</p><pre><code>\nNote: In the CSS Color Module Level 4 spec, rgba() has been defined as an legacy function with identical grammar and behaviour to rgb(); in effect, an alias. Going forward, both can accept exactly the same parameters.\n\n Hexadecimal notation #RRGGBB, #RGB\n \n \n "#", followed by six hexadecimal characters (0-9, A-F), where the first two digits represent the red part, the second two the green part and the last two the blue part.\n "#", followed by three hexadecimal characters (0-9, A-F), where the first digit represents the red part, the second the green part and the last one the blue part.\n \n The three-digit RGB notation (#RGB) and the six-digit form (#RRGGBB) are equal, for example #f03 and #ff0033 represent the same color.\n Functional Notation rgb(R,G,B)\n "rgb", followed by three <integer> or three <percentage> values, plus an optional alpha value that specifies the transparency of the color (this can be an <integer> between 0 and 1, or a <percentage>)\n The integer number 255 corresponds to 100%, and to F or FF in the hexadecimal notation.\n/* These examples all specify the same RGB color: */\n \n#f03\n#F03\n#ff0033\n#FF0033\nrgb(255,0,51)\nrgb(255, 0, 51)\nrgb(255, 0, 51.2) /* ERROR! Don't use fractions, use integers */ \nrgb(100%,0%,20%)\nrgb(100%, 0%, 20%)\nrgb(100%, 0, 20%) /* ERROR! Don't mix up integer and percentage notation */\n\n/* whitespace syntax */\nrgb(255 0 0)\n\n/* optional alpha value */\nrgb(255,0,0,0.4) /* 40% opaque red */ \nrgb(255,0,0,40%) /* 40% opaque red with percentage value for alpha */ \nrgb(255 0 0 / 0.4) /* 40% opaque red */ \nrgb(255 0 0 / 40%) /* 40% opaque red with percentage value for alpha */ \n\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/color_value#rgb()
rgba()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>Colors can be defined in the Red-green-blue-alpha model (RGBa) in two ways:</p><pre><code>\n Hexadecimal notation #RRGGBBAA and #RGBA\n \n \n "#", followed by eight hexadecimal characters (0-9, A-F), where the first two digits represent the red part, the second two the green part, the third two the blue part and the last two the transparency.\n "#", followed by four hexadecimal characters (0-9, A-F), where the first digit represents the red part, the second the green part, the third one the blue part and the last one the transparency.\n \n The four-digit RGB notation (#RGBA) and the eight-digit form (#RRGGBBAA) are equal, for example, #f038 and #ff003388 represent the same color.\n using the rgba() functional notation.\n RGBa extends the RGB color model to include the alpha channel, allowing specification of the opacity of a color.\n a means opacity: 0=transparent; 1=opaque;\n#f030 /* 0% opaque red */ \n#F03F /* full opaque red */ \n#ff003300 /* 0% opaque red */ \n#FF003388 /* 50% opaque red */ \nrgba(255,0,0,0.1) /* 10% opaque red */ \nrgba(255,0,0,0.4) /* 40% opaque red */ \nrgba(255,0,0,0.7) /* 70% opaque red */ \nrgba(255,0,0, 1) /* full opaque red */ \n\n/* whitespace syntax */\nrgba(255 0 0 / 0.4) /* 40% opaque red */ \n\n/* percentage value for alpha */\nrgba(255 0 0 / 40%) /* 40% opaque red */ \n\nNote: In the CSS Color Module Level 4 spec, rgba() has been defined as an legacy function with identical grammar and behaviour to rgb(); in effect, an alias. Going forward, both can accept exactly the same parameters.\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/color_value#rgba()

rotate()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>The rotate() CSS function defines a transformation that moves the element around a fixed point (as specified by the transform-origin property) without deforming it. A rotation by 180° is called point reflection.</p><pre><code>rotate(a)\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/transform-function/rotate

skew()	A			css functions							<section class="prog__container"><p>The skew() CSS function is a shear mapping, or transvection, distorting each point of an element by a certain angle in each direction. The more far from the origin, the more away the point is, the greater will be the value added to it.</p><pre><code>skew(ax) or\nskew(ax, ay)\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/transform-function/skew

symbols()	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The symbols() function allows counter styles to be defined inline, directly as the value of the CSS property. The symbols() function doesn't have all the capabilities and options of the @counter-style at-rule, but is useful in cases such as when the style is used only once and you don't need all the the options provided by @counter-style.</p><pre><code>symbols() = symbols( ? [ | ]+ );</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/symbols

The CSS syntax reflects this goal and its basic building blocks are:</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Syntax

text-combine-upright	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The text-combine-upright CSS property specifies the combination of multiple characters into the space of a single character. If the combined text is wider than 1em, the user agent must fit the contents within 1em. The resulting composition is treated as a single upright glyph for layout and decoration. This property only has an effect in vertical writing modes.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>none</em></p><pre><code>/* Keyword values */\ntext-combine-upright: none;\ntext-combine-upright: all;\n\n/* Digits values */\ntext-combine-upright: digits; /* fits 2 consecutive digits horizontally inside vertical text */\ntext-combine-upright: digits 4; /* fits up to 4 consecutive digits horizontally inside vertical text */\n\n/* Global values */\ntext-combine-upright: inherit;\ntext-combine-upright: initial;\ntext-combine-upright: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/text-combine-upright

text-emphasis	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The text-emphasis CSS property is a shorthand property for setting text-emphasis-style and text-emphasis-color in one declaration. This property will apply the specified emphasis mark to each character of the element's text, except separator characters, like spaces,  and control characters.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>text-emphasis-style: none</li><li>text-emphasis-color: currentColor</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* Initial value */\ntext-emphasis: none; /* No emphasis marks */\n\n/* <string> value */\ntext-emphasis: 'x';\ntext-emphasis: '点';\ntext-emphasis: '\25B2';\ntext-emphasis: '*' #555;\ntext-emphasis: 'foo'; /* Should NOT use. transform-origin	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The transform-origin property lets you modify the origin for transformations of an element. transition	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The transition CSS property is a shorthand property for transition-property, transition-duration, transition-timing-function, and transition-delay. It enables you to define the transition between two states of an element. Different states may be defined using pseudo-classes like :hover or :active or dynamically set using JavaScript.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>as each of the properties of the shorthand:<ul><li>transition-delay: 0s</li><li>transition-duration: 0s</li><li>transition-property: all</li><li>transition-timing-function: ease</li></ul></em></p><pre><code>/* Apply to 1 property */\n/* property name | duration */\ntransition: margin-left 4s;\n\n/* property name | duration | delay */\ntransition: margin-left 4s 1s;\n\n/* property name | duration | timing function | delay */\ntransition: margin-left 4s ease-in-out 1s;\n\n/* Apply to 2 properties */\ntransition: margin-left 4s, color 1s;\n\n/* Apply to all changed properties */\ntransition: all 0.5s ease-out;\n\n/* Global values */\ntransition: inherit;\ntransition: initial;\ntransition: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/transition

turn	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>turn represents the number of turns the angle is. One full circle is 1turn. unicode-bidi	A			css properties							<section class="prog__container"><p>The unicode-bidi CSS property together with the direction property relates to the handling of bidirectional text in a document. For example, if a block of text contains both left-to-right and right-to-left text then the user-agent uses a complex Unicode algorithm to decide how to display the text. This property overrides this algorithm and allows the developer to control the text embedding.</p><p><b>Initial Value: </b><em>normal</em></p><pre><code>/* Keyword values */\nunicode-bidi: normal;\nunicode-bidi: embed;\nunicode-bidi: isolate;\nunicode-bidi: bidi-override;\nunicode-bidi: isolate-override;\nunicode-bidi: plaintext;\n\n/* Global values */\nunicode-bidi: inherit;\nunicode-bidi: initial;\nunicode-bidi: unset;\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/unicode-bidi

unicode-range	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The unicode-range CSS descriptor sets the specific range of characters to be used from a font defined by @font-face and made available for use on the current page. If the page doesn't use any character in this range, the font is not downloaded; if it uses at least one, the whole font is downloaded.</p><pre><code>/* <unicode-range> values */\nunicode-range: U+26; /* single codepoint */\nunicode-range: U+0-7F;\nunicode-range: U+0025-00FF; /* codepoint range */\nunicode-range: U+4??; /* wildcard range */\nunicode-range: U+0025-00FF, U+4??; /* multiple values */\n</code></pre></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/@font-face/unicode-range

Omitting the asterisk with simple selectors has the same effect. For instance, *.warning and .warning are considered equal.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Universal_selectors
unset	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>The unset CSS keyword is the combination of the initial and inherit keywords. Like these two other CSS-wide keywords, it can be applied to any CSS property, including the CSS shorthand all. This keyword resets the property to its inherited value if it inherits from its parent or to its initial value if not. In other words, it behaves like the inherit keyword in the first case and like the initial keyword in the second case.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/unset

For some properties, used values can be retrieved by calling window.getComputedStyle. Dimensions (e.g., width, line-height) are all in pixels, shorthand properties (e.g., background) are consistent with their component properties (e.g., background-color, display) and consistent with position and float, and every CSS property has a value.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/used_value

value definition syntax	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>Sign\n   Name\n   Description\n   Example\n  \n \n \n  \n   Combinators\n  \n  \n    \n   Juxtaposition\n   Components are mandatory and should appear in that order\n   solid <length>\n  \n  \n   &&\n   Double ampersand\n   Components are mandatory but may appear in any order\n   <length> && <string>\n  \n  \n   ||\n   Double bar\n   At least one of the components must be present, and they may appear in any order.\n   <'border-image-outset'> || <'border-image-slice'>\n  \n  \n   |\n   Single bar\n   Exactly one of the components must be present\n   smaller | small | normal | big | bigger\n  \n  \n   [ ]\n   Brackets\n   Group components to bypass precedence rules\n   bold [ thin && <length> ]\n  \n  \n   Multipliers\n  \n  \n    \n   No multiplier\n   Exactly 1 times\n   solid\n  \n  \n   *\n   Asterisk\n   0 or more times\n   bold smaller*\n  \n  \n   +\n   Plus sign\n   1 or more times\n   bold smaller+\n  \n  \n   ?\n   Question mark\n   0 or 1 time (that is optional)\n   bold smaller?\n  \n  \n   {A,B}\n   Curly braces\n   At least A times, at most B times\n   bold smaller{1,3}\n  \n  \n   #\n   Hash mark\n   1 or more times, but each occurrence separated by a comma (',')\n   bold smaller#\n  \n  \n   !\n   Exclamation point\n   Group must produce at least 1 value\n   [ bold? smaller? ]!</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Value_definition_syntax

visual formatting model	A										<section class="prog__container"><p>Another case that leads to the creation of anonymous block boxes is an inline box that contains one or several block boxes. In that case, the box containing the block box is split into two inline boxes - one before and one after the block box. All the inline boxes before the block box are then enclosed into an anonymous block box, so are the inline boxes following the block box. Therefore, the block box becomes the sibling of the two anonymous block boxes containing the inline elements.</p></section>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Visual_formatting_model
